			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<p><b>Chipotle Mexican Grill, Inc.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/tʃ/: 'ch' in 'China'">tʃ</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">chih-<span style="font-size:90%">POHT</span>-lay</i></a>),<sup id="cite_ref-barnes_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barnes-7">[7]</a></sup> often known simply as <b>Chipotle</b>, is an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> chain of <a href="/wiki/Fast_casual" class="mw-redirect" title="Fast casual">fast casual</a> restaurants in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-london_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-london-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-annual_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annual-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ts-2008aug13_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ts-2008aug13-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Genuss-2013jun06_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genuss-2013jun06-11">[11]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-lexpress-2012may31_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lexpress-2012may31-12">[12]</a></sup> specializing in <a href="/wiki/Taco" title="Taco">tacos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mission_burrito" title="Mission burrito">Mission-style</a><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Burrito" title="Burrito">burritos</a>. Its name derives from <i><a href="/wiki/Chipotle" title="Chipotle">chipotle</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a> name for a smoked and dried <a href="/wiki/Jalape%C3%B1o" title="Jalapeño">jalapeño</a> <a href="/wiki/Chili_pepper" title="Chili pepper">chili pepper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>  The company trades on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> under the ticker symbol CMG.<sup id="cite_ref-rocky2-founder_16-0" class="reference"><a class="nowrap"><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> US$1.402 billion <small>(2016)</small><sup id="cite_ref-10K2012_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K2012-4">[4]</a></sup></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">64,570<sup id="cite_ref-Chipotle's_Recipe_for_Success_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chipotle's_Recipe_for_Success-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chipotle_Investor_Relations_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chipotle_Investor_Relations-6">[6]</a></sup> (2017)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pizzeria_Locale" class="mw-redirect" title="Pizzeria Locale">Pizzeria Locale</a> (2013–present)</li><li><a href="/wiki/ShopHouse_Southeast_Asian_Kitchen" title="ShopHouse Southeast Asian Kitchen">ShopHouse Southeast Asian Kitchen</a> (2011–2017)</li><li><a href="/wiki/Tasty_Made" title="Tasty Made">Tasty Made</a> (2016–2018)</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.chipotle.com">www<wbr></wbr>.chipotle<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Chipotle is one of the first chains of <a href="/wiki/Fast_casual_restaurant" title="Fast casual restaurant">fast casual</a> dining establishments.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Competitors in the fast-casual Mexican market include <a href="/wiki/Qdoba_Mexican_Grill" class="mw-redirect" title="Qdoba Mexican Grill">Qdoba Mexican Grill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moe%27s_Southwest_Grill" title="Moe's Southwest Grill">Moe's Southwest Grill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rubio%27s_Coastal_Grill" title="Rubio's Coastal Grill">Rubio's Coastal Grill</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baja_Fresh" title="Baja Fresh">Baja Fresh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p><p>Founded by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ells" title="Steve Ells">Steve Ells</a> on July 13, 1993, Chipotle had 16 restaurants (all in <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>) when <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonald's Corporation">McDonald's Corporation</a> became a major investor in 1998. By the time McDonald's fully divested itself from Chipotle in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-rocky_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocky-19">[19]</a></sup> the chain had grown to over 500 locations.
</p><p>With more than 2,000 locations, Chipotle had a net income of US$475.6 million and a staff of more than 45,000 employees in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-cmgearnings2015_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmgearnings2015-3">[3]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2018, Chipotle announced the relocation of their corporate headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach,_California" title="Newport Beach, California">Newport Beach, California</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>, ending their relationship with Denver after 25 years.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg/220px-University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg/220px-University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Denver_campus_pics_107.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first Chipotle, near the campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a></div></div></div>
<p>Founder Steve Ells attended <a href="/wiki/The_Culinary_Institute_of_America" title="The Culinary Institute of America">the Culinary Institute of America</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_New_York" title="Hyde Park, New York">Hyde Park, New York</a>. Afterward, he became a line cook for <a href="/wiki/Jeremiah_Tower" title="Jeremiah Tower">Jeremiah Tower</a> at <a href="/wiki/Stars_(restaurant)" title="Stars (restaurant)">Stars</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parrish_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parrish-20">[20]</a></sup> There, Ells observed the popularity of the <a href="/wiki/Taquer%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Taquería">taquerías</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mission_burrito" title="Mission burrito">San Francisco burritos</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mission_District,_San_Francisco" title="Mission District, San Francisco">Mission District</a>. In 1993, Ells took what he learned in San Francisco<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and opened the first Chipotle Mexican Grill in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, in a former <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Madison" title="Dolly Madison">Dolly Madison</a> Ice Cream store at 1644 East Evans Avenue,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a> campus, using an $85,000 loan from his father.<sup id="cite_ref-rocky_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocky-19">[19]</a></sup> Ells and his father calculated that the store would need to sell 107 burritos per day to be profitable. After one month, the original restaurant was selling over 1,000 burritos a day.<sup id="cite_ref-rocky2-founder_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocky2-founder-16">[16]</a></sup> The second store opened in 1995 using Chipotle's <a href="/wiki/Cash_flow" title="Cash flow">cash flow</a>, and the third was opened using an <a href="/wiki/Small_Business_Administration" title="Small Business Administration">SBA</a> loan. To fund more growth, Ells' father invested $1.5 million. Afterwards, Ells created a <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board of directors</a> and business plan, raising an additional $1.8 million for the company.<sup id="cite_ref-obsession_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obsession-23">[23]</a></sup> Ells had originally planned to use funds from the first Chipotle to open a fine-dining restaurant, but instead focused on Chipotle Mexican Grill when the restaurants saw success.<sup id="cite_ref-Wall_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wall-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p><p>In 1998, the first restaurant outside of Colorado opened in <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City, Missouri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The company opened its first location in Minnesota by opening near the campus of the University of Minnesota in Minneapolis in March 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-1999feb28_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-1999feb28-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>In 1998, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> made an initial minority investment in the company. By 2001, the company had grown to be Chipotle's largest investor.<sup id="cite_ref-rocky_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocky-19">[19]</a></sup> The investment from McDonald's allowed the firm to quickly expand, from 16 restaurants in 1998 to over 500 by 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> On January 26, 2006, Chipotle made its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO) after increasing the share price twice due to high pre-IPO demand. In its first day as a public company, the stock rose exactly 100%, resulting in the best U.S.-based IPO in six years, and the second-best IPO for a restaurant after <a href="/wiki/Boston_Market" title="Boston Market">Boston Market</a>. The money from the offering was then used to fund new store growth.<sup id="cite_ref-rocky2-feeding_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocky2-feeding-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2005, Monty Moran was appointed president and chief operating officer of Chipotle while founder Steve Ells remained chairman and CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2006dec15_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2006dec15-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2006, McDonald's fully divested from Chipotle.<sup id="cite_ref-buzz_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buzz-31">[31]</a></sup> This was part of a larger initiative for McDonald's to divest all of its non-core business restaurants — Chipotle, <a href="/wiki/Donatos_Pizza" title="Donatos Pizza">Donatos Pizza</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Market" title="Boston Market">Boston Market</a> — so that it could focus on the main McDonald's chain.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> McDonald's had invested approximately $360 million into Chipotle, and took out $1.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-obsession_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obsession-23">[23]</a></sup> McDonald's had attempted to get Chipotle to add drive-through windows and a breakfast menu, which Ells resisted.<sup id="cite_ref-bn-2015feb02_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-2015feb02-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tmf-2015dec27_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmf-2015dec27-34">[34]</a></sup>  In 2008, Chipotle opened its first location outside of the United States in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ts-2008aug13_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ts-2008aug13-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2009, president and chief operating officer Monty Moran was promoted to co-CEO, a position that he would share with Steve Ells, while Moran retained his president position.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters-2009jan05_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-2009jan05-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>In a list of fastest-growing restaurant chains in 2009, Chipotle was ranked eighth, based on increases in U.S. sales over the past year,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and in 2010 Chipotle was ranked third.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a></i> ranked Chipotle as the best Mexican fast-food chain in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The company serves approximately 750,000 customers per day.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2010, Chipotle hired chef Nate Appleman to develop new cuisine. Appleman has won <a href="/wiki/James_Beard_Foundation_Award" title="James Beard Foundation Award">Rising Star Chef</a> from the <a href="/wiki/James_Beard_Foundation" title="James Beard Foundation">James Beard Foundation</a>, was named "Best New Chef" by the <a href="/wiki/Food_%26_Wine" title="Food &amp; Wine">Food &amp; Wine</a> magazine, and competed on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Iron_Chef" title="The Next Iron Chef">The Next Iron Chef</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement" title="U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement">U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement</a> (ICE) audited Chipotle's Minneapolis restaurants, and found that some employees had been hired using fraudulent documents. In December, Chipotle fired 450 employees from its Minneapolis restaurants as a result of the audit, resulting in protests by local groups.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In February 2011, ICE expanded the audit to include 60 restaurants in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> which resulted in 40 workers being fired. In April 2011, the criminal division of the Attorney General's office in Washington, D.C., joined the case, and ICE agents began interviewing employees at 20 to 25 restaurants in other locations, such as <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In response to the government investigations, Chipotle hired former director of ICE <a href="/wiki/Julie_Myers" title="Julie Myers">Julie Myers Wood</a> and high-profile attorneys <a href="/wiki/Robert_Luskin" title="Robert Luskin">Robert Luskin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gregory_B._Craig" title="Gregory B. Craig">Gregory B. Craig</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2016, Chipotle announced that co-CEO Monty Moran has stepped down from his role effective immediately with Steve Ells becoming the sole CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-bi-2016dec12_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bi-2016dec12-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tmf-2016dec14_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmf-2016dec14-47">[47]</a></sup> Eleven months later, founder Steve Ells announced in November 2017 that he would be stepping down as CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-ReplaceFounder_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReplaceFounder-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2017, Chipotle announced it signed a 15-year lease and in late 2018 will move around 450 corporate employees - currently housed in multiple buildings around downtown Denver - into the new 1144 Fifteenth Tower and occupy around 126,000 square feet or 5 floors of the 40-story tower.
</p><p>In February 2018, Chipotle announced that Taco Bell CEO Brian Niccol would replace Steve Ells as CEO starting on March 5 while Ellis would retain his chairman position.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2018feb13_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2018feb13-49">[49]</a></sup> Many industry analysts praised Niccol's appointment saying that Chipotle "needed new blood."<sup id="cite_ref-ut-2018feb13_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ut-2018feb13-50">[50]</a></sup> Chipotle stock went up $30.27, or 12.04%, as a result of the announcement. However, other analysts criticized the announcement by saying that "the move goes against everything the burrito chain stands for."<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc-2018feb14_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc-2018feb14-51">[51]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2018, Chipotle announced that it would relocate headquarters from Denver to <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach,_California" title="Newport Beach, California">Newport Beach, California</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. Corporate functions handled in their Denver and New York offices would move to Newport Beach or to an existing office in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>. This move would impact 400 workers, some being offered relocation and retention packages.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2018, under new CEO Brian Niccol, the company announced the closing of 65 under-performing restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_restaurant_expansion">Other restaurant expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Other restaurant expansion" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, Steve Ells was a judge for the TV show <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Next_Great_Restaurant" title="America's Next Great Restaurant">America's Next Great Restaurant</a></i> and investor of <a href="/wiki/Soul_Daddy" title="Soul Daddy">ANGR Holdings</a>, the company that will be running the winning concept's restaurants. Chipotle has agreed to purchase Ells' investment in ANGR at his cost, provide support for ANGR operations, and invest a total of $2.3 million in cash contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The winning concept, <a href="/wiki/Soul_Daddy" title="Soul Daddy">Soul Daddy</a>, was quickly closed after operating for less than 5 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-MOACLOSURE_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOACLOSURE-56">[56]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2011, Chipotle opened an <a href="/wiki/Asian_cuisine" title="Asian cuisine">Asian</a> fast-casual concept restaurant named <a href="/wiki/ShopHouse_Southeast_Asian_Kitchen" title="ShopHouse Southeast Asian Kitchen">ShopHouse Southeast Asian Kitchen</a> in Washington, D.C.<sup id="cite_ref-shophouse_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shophouse-57">[57]</a></sup> The company has said the new restaurant "would follow the Chipotle service format and its focus on 'food with integrity' in ingredients."<sup id="cite_ref-Jennings_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jennings-58">[58]</a></sup> Chipotle's plan was to start with only one store, and see how the restaurant works out before expanding the concept.<sup id="cite_ref-Anderson_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>On December 18, 2013, the company revealed that it had opened its first fast-food pizza chain in Denver back in May 2013. According to <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>, Chipotle partnered with a local full-service restaurant called Pizzeria Locale to create a fast-food version of the eatery, keeping its name. The company plans to open at least two more pizzerias in the Denver area.<sup id="cite_ref-nmx_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmx-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2014, Chipotle announced an increase in menu prices for the first time in nearly three years, due to increasing costs for steak, avocados, and cheese. The price increase was expected to be rolled out from the end of second quarter of 2014 through the end of the third quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In late 2015, Chipotle expanded its mobile strategy through delivery partnerships with tech startups like <a href="/wiki/Tapingo" title="Tapingo">Tapingo</a>, a delivery service that targets college campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p><p>On July 29, 2016, the company announced the opening of its first <a href="/wiki/Tasty_Made" title="Tasty Made">Tasty Made</a> burger restaurant in the fall. Chipotle was still dealing with the various virus outbreaks with additional marketing. The company was also reducing the number of new stores for the year from 235 to 220.<sup id="cite_ref-lat_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-63">[63]</a></sup></p><p>The newer restaurant concepts did not perform as well as expected so that ShopHouse Southeast Asian Kitchen and Tasty Made were respectively closed in March 2017<sup id="cite_ref-eater-2017mar09_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2017mar09-64">[64]</a></sup> and February 2018<sup id="cite_ref-eater-2018mar01_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2018mar01-65">[65]</a></sup> leaving only Pizzeria Locale operating besides the parent company.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: International" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_London_Baker_St.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Chipotle_London_Baker_St.jpg/170px-Chipotle_London_Baker_St.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="190" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2597" data-file-height="2903"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 190px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Chipotle_London_Baker_St.jpg/170px-Chipotle_London_Baker_St.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="190" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_London_Baker_St.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The second Chipotle Mexican Grill location in London, located on <a href="/wiki/Baker_Street" title="Baker Street">Baker Street</a></div></div></div>
<p>According to an article in <a href="/wiki/The_Motley_Fool" title="The Motley Fool">The Motley Fool</a>, Chipotle had 17 locations outside of the United States by October 2014 with the majority in Canada, and the UK was in the process of opening more locations.<sup id="cite_ref-tmf-2014oct17_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmf-2014oct17-66">[66]</a></sup> The rate of overseas expansion was slower than expected.<sup id="cite_ref-tgam-2010aug16_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgam-2010aug16-67">[67]</a></sup>  Many of the press reviewers thought that the food was overpriced for their area.<sup id="cite_ref-lexpress-2012may31_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lexpress-2012may31-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Genuss-2013oct14_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genuss-2013oct14-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2018 there are 33 locations outside of the United States with 19 locations in Canada (Ottawa, Toronto, Markham, Vaughan, Mississauga, Oakville, Vancouver),  6 locations in The United Kingdom (London), 6 in France (Paris), and 2 in Germany (Frankfurt).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="numbers not supported by current refs (February 2017)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-cmgearnings2015_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmgearnings2015-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes-2013feb05_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-2013feb05-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Canada" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In August 2008, Chipotle opened its first location outside of the United States in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ts-2008aug13_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ts-2008aug13-10">[10]</a></sup> The second location in Toronto–and in all of Canada–was not opened until 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-tgam-2010aug16_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgam-2010aug16-67">[67]</a></sup></p><p>The first Canadian location outside of the Toronto area was opened in Vancouver in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-biv-2012dec13_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biv-2012dec13-70">[70]</a></sup> A second Vancouver-area location was opened in <a href="/wiki/Burnaby" title="Burnaby">Burnaby</a> in October 2014<sup id="cite_ref-604now-2014oct02_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-604now-2014oct02-71">[71]</a></sup> followed by a third in <a href="/wiki/Surrey,_British_Columbia" title="Surrey, British Columbia">Surrey</a> in January 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-604now-2016jan29_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-604now-2016jan29-72">[72]</a></sup> a fourth in <a href="/wiki/Langley,_British_Columbia_(district_municipality)" title="Langley, British Columbia (district municipality)">Langley</a> in October 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-604now-2016oct10_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-604now-2016oct10-73">[73]</a></sup> and a fifth in <a href="/wiki/West_Vancouver" title="West Vancouver">West Vancouver</a> in March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-dh-2017jan30_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dh-2017jan30-74">[74]</a></sup></p><p>The first location in the nation's capital of <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a> was opened in February 2017 at the <a href="/wiki/Rideau_Centre" title="Rideau Centre">Rideau Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cn-2017feb02_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cn-2017feb02-75">[75]</a></sup></p><p>Chipotle rapidly expanded in the Greater Toronto area, and is still opening new locations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Is this an opinion? If the (unsupported) numbers giving in the same paragraph are correct for GTA, that would average one new restaurant opening per year, which is not very rapid when compared to similar sized cities in the U.S. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> As of 2018, there are 11 locations in Toronto, 2 in Vaughan, 2 in Mississauga, 1 in Oakville, and 1 location in Markham.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: United Kingdom" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Chipotle expanded to Europe with the first European restaurant opening in May 2010 in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-london_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-london-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ti-2010jun05_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ti-2010jun05-77">[77]</a></sup> A second location opened in London in September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-bighospitality-2011sep02_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bighospitality-2011sep02-78">[78]</a></sup> The following year, three additional locations were quickly opened in the London area.<sup id="cite_ref-bighospitality-2012mar13_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bighospitality-2012mar13-79">[79]</a></sup> After this growth spurt, the rate of further expansion in London slowed greatly with the sixth location appearing in 2013<sup id="cite_ref-bighospitality-2012sep20_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bighospitality-2012sep20-80">[80]</a></sup> and the seventh in June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-bighospitality-2015apr13_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bighospitality-2015apr13-81">[81]</a></sup> Although Chipotle blames the slow growth in the United Kingdom on the British unfamiliarity with Mexican foods,<sup id="cite_ref-bn-2013feb26_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-2013feb26-82">[82]</a></sup> several locally owned burrito chains had opened locations across the United Kingdom during the same interval.<sup id="cite_ref-bn-2013apr23_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn-2013apr23-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: France" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The first location in France opened in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> in May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-lexpress-2012may31_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lexpress-2012may31-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10q_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10q-84">[84]</a></sup></p><p>Expansion in France was much slower than that in the United Kingdom or Canada, with a second location in Paris opening in 2013<sup id="cite_ref-fastandfood-2013oct15_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastandfood-2013oct15-85">[85]</a></sup> and a third location in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-lexpress-2014dec27_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lexpress-2014dec27-86">[86]</a></sup> At 7,000 square feet, the restaurant at La Défense is, as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the largest Chipotle location in the world, while a typical Chipotle restaurant is usually between 2,200 and 2,500 square feet.<sup id="cite_ref-mm-2014mar05_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mm-2014mar05-87">[87]</a></sup> A fourth Parisian location was opened in <a href="/wiki/Levallois-Perret" title="Levallois-Perret">Levallois-Perret</a> in 2015<sup id="cite_ref-lcn-2015sep16_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcn-2015sep16-88">[88]</a></sup> followed by a fifth<sup id="cite_ref-tokster-2016may24_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokster-2016may24-89">[89]</a></sup> and a sixth<sup id="cite_ref-lb-2016sep14_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lb-2016sep14-90">[90]</a></sup> Parisian location in 2016, both in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Germain-des-Pr%C3%A9s" title="Saint-Germain-des-Prés">Saint-Germain-des-Prés</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Germany" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The first location in Germany opened up in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Skyline_Plaza_(Frankfurt)" title="Skyline Plaza (Frankfurt)">Skyline Plaza</a> shopping mall in August 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Genuss-2013jun06_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genuss-2013jun06-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Genuss-2013oct14_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genuss-2013oct14-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>Second location opened in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/MyZeil" title="MyZeil">MyZeil</a> shopping mall in April 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_management">Corporate management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Corporate management" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>Chipotle's team includes a residing corporate office of managers and its board of directors. Members of both teams are appointed to serve on committees: audit, compensation, and nominating and corporate governance.
</p><p>The top management team consists of the Chief Executive Officer, Steve Ells; the Chief Financial Officer, Jack R. Hartung; the Chief Marketing and Development Officer, Mark Crumpacker.<sup id="cite_ref-Chipotle:_Investor_Relations_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chipotle:_Investor_Relations-92">[92]</a></sup> The current board of directors consists of: Steve Ells, Patrick Flynn, Albert Baldocchi, Neil Flanzraich, Darlene Friedman, Stephen Gillet, Kimbal Musk and John Charlesworth.<sup id="cite_ref-Chipotle:_Board_of_Directors_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chipotle:_Board_of_Directors-93">[93]</a></sup>  On March 14, 2018 it was reported that Mark Crumpacker, who had previously been charged in a 2016 cocaine ring indictment, would be leaving the company.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>Founder Steve Ells serves as <a href="/wiki/Chairman" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman">chairman</a> of the company, and served as <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">Chief executive officer</a> until November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReplaceFounder_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReplaceFounder-48">[48]</a></sup> He has a 1.25% stake in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-reklaitis_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reklaitis-96">[96]</a></sup> The labor-market research firm Glassdoor reported that Steve Ells earned $29 million in 2014, versus a median of $19,000 for Chipotle's workers, making the CEO-to-worker pay ratio 1522:1.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p><p>On February 13, 2018, Chipotle announced that Taco Bell CEO Brian Niccol would replace Steve Ells as CEO starting on March 5 while Ells would retain his chairman position.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2018feb13_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2018feb13-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_and_distribution">Operation and distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Operation and distribution" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>All of Chipotle's restaurants are company-owned, rather than <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchised</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tampa_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tampa-98">[98]</a></sup> As of December 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 1430 restaurants have since opened throughout the United States and Canada, with locations in 43 states, Ontario, British Columbia, and the District of Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-10klocations_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10klocations-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>The field team are the employees who work closely with but not directly within specific restaurants. The field support system includes apprentice team leaders (step up from restaurateurs), team leaders or area managers, team directors and regional directors (not atypical for them to oversee more than fifty locations).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Because Chipotle does not franchise, all restaurants are corporately owned. Thus, whenever Chipotle is in the process of launching a new location, the field team hires a new general manager and trains them at a current location so that they will be ready for the new location when it opens for business. The corporate office takes care of finding and funding new locations as well.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Menu">Menu</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Menu" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Brandon.jpeg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Chipotle_Brandon.jpeg/220px-Chipotle_Brandon.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Chipotle_Brandon.jpeg/220px-Chipotle_Brandon.jpeg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Brandon.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Chipotle restaurant in Brandon, Florida, having the typical service-line layout with menu above</div></div></div><p>
Chipotle's menu consists of five items: <a href="/wiki/Burrito" title="Burrito">burritos</a>, bowls, <a href="/wiki/Taco" title="Taco">tacos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quesadilla" title="Quesadilla">quesadillas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salads</a>. The price of each item is based on the choice of chicken, pork <a href="/wiki/Carnitas" title="Carnitas">carnitas</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Barbacoa" title="Barbacoa">barbacoa</a>, steak, <a href="/wiki/Carne_asada" title="Carne asada">carne asada</a>, tofu-based "sofritas",<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> or vegetarian (with guacamole, which would be at an extra charge otherwise). Additional optional toppings are offered free of charge, including: rice, beans, four types of <a href="/wiki/Salsa_(sauce)" title="Salsa (sauce)">salsa</a>, sour cream, cheese, and lettuce.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ingred_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ingred-106">[106]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Chips_and_Queso.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Chipotle_Chips_and_Queso.jpg/220px-Chipotle_Chips_and_Queso.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Chipotle_Chips_and_Queso.jpg/220px-Chipotle_Chips_and_Queso.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Chips_and_Queso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chipotle regular sized chips and queso with a side of sour cream.</div></div></div><p> When asked in 2007 about expanding the menu, Steve Ells said, "[I]t's important to keep the menu focused, because if you just do a few things, you can ensure that you do them better than anybody else."<sup id="cite_ref-integ_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-integ-107">[107]</a></sup> Chipotle also offers a children's menu.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Most restaurants sell <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margarita" title="Margarita">margaritas</a> in addition to <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a> and fruit drinks.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p><p>The majority of food is prepared in each restaurant. Some exceptions are the beans and carnitas, which are prepared at a central kitchen in <a href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago, Illinois</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-111">[111]</a></sup> None of the restaurants have <a href="/wiki/Refrigerator" title="Refrigerator">freezers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microwave_oven" title="Microwave oven">microwave ovens</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Can_opener" title="Can opener">can openers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burrito_Bowl.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Burrito_Bowl.jpg/220px-Burrito_Bowl.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Burrito_Bowl.jpg/220px-Burrito_Bowl.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burrito_Bowl.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chicken Burrito Bowl</div></div></div>
<p>The chain experimented with breakfast foods at two airports in the <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">Washington (D.C.) metropolitan area</a> but decided against expanding the menu in that direction.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bi-2015apr10_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bi-2015apr10-115">[115]</a></sup> Starting in 2009, selected restaurants had offered a <a href="/wiki/Pozole" title="Pozole">pozole</a> soup,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-westword-2009apr16_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-westword-2009apr16-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ccb-2011jan11_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccb-2011jan11-118">[118]</a></sup> which has since been discontinued.
</p><p>In June 2015, Chipotle began test marketing a pork and chicken <a href="/wiki/Chorizo" title="Chorizo">chorizo</a>-type sausage as a new protein option at selected locations in the Kansas City area.<sup id="cite_ref-fnc-2015jun04_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fnc-2015jun04-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eater-2015jun02_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2015jun02-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kcs-2015jun02_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcs-2015jun02-121">[121]</a></sup> Some food writers have expressed their health related concerns over the protein's relatively high sodium content since a 4-ounce serving contains 293 calories and 803 milligrams of sodium<sup id="cite_ref-kcs-2015jun03_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcs-2015jun03-122">[122]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/American_Heart_Association" title="American Heart Association">American Heart Association</a>’s recommended daily amount is less than 1,500 milligrams of sodium.<sup id="cite_ref-american_heart_assn_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-american_heart_assn-123">[123]</a></sup> In contrast, the protein options with next highest sodium contents are Barbacoa with 530 milligrams and sofritas with 555 milligrams.<sup id="cite_ref-kcs-2015jun03_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kcs-2015jun03-122">[122]</a></sup> An earlier version on the Mexican sausage was tested in Denver and New York City in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-hp-2011jun29_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hp-2011jun29-124">[124]</a></sup> but that test was terminated when that version of the sausage was perceived as looking too greasy.<sup id="cite_ref-ct-2015jun02_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-2015jun02-125">[125]</a></sup>  Chorizo was discontinued in September 2017<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> but was returned to the menu in the following year for a limited time.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>Chipotle accepts <a href="/wiki/Fax" title="Fax">fax</a> orders, and in 2005 the company added the ability to order online from their website. For both online and fax orders, customers proceed to the front of the line to pay for pre-ordered food.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> In 2009, Chipotle released an <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">app</a> for the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> that allows users to find nearby Chipotle locations, place an order, and prepay with a credit card.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In 2013, Chipotle released an <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Android</a> app that allows users to locate nearby Chipotle locations, place an order, prepay with a credit or gift card, and access favorites and recent orders.<sup id="cite_ref-androidandme1_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-androidandme1-130">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-androidpolice1_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-androidpolice1-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Nutrition">Nutrition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Nutrition" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2003, a <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Science_in_the_Public_Interest" title="Center for Science in the Public Interest">Center for Science in the Public Interest</a> report stated that Chipotle's burritos contain over 1,000 calories, which is nearly equivalent to two meals' worth of food.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a> Health.com placed the burritos on their list of the "20 Worst Foods in America" because of their high caloric content and high sodium.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> When a burrito with carnitas, rice, vegetables, cheese, guacamole, and salsa was compared with a typical <a href="/wiki/Big_Mac" title="Big Mac">Big Mac</a>, the burrito had more fat, cholesterol, carbohydrates, and sodium than the Big Mac, but it also had more protein and fiber.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The restaurant has also received praise – Health.com included the restaurant in its list of the "Healthiest Fast Food Restaurants".<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p><p>Chipotle's vegetarian options include rice, black beans, fajita vegetables (onions and bell peppers), salsa, guacamole and cheese.<sup id="cite_ref-special_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-special-137">[137]</a></sup>  All items other than the meats, cheese, sour cream, and honey vinaigrette dressing are <a href="/wiki/Veganism" title="Veganism">vegan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-special_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-special-137">[137]</a></sup> As of late 2013, Chipotle developed a new cooking strategy for the <a href="/wiki/Pinto_bean" title="Pinto bean">pinto beans</a>, eliminating the bacon and making them vegetarian and vegan-friendly.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The cheese is processed with vegetable-based <a href="/wiki/Rennet" title="Rennet">rennet</a> in order to be suitable for vegetarians.<sup id="cite_ref-special_137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-special-137">[137]</a></sup>  In April 2010, Chipotle began testing a vegan "Garden Blend" option, which is a plant-based <a href="/wiki/Meat_analogue" title="Meat analogue">meat alternative</a> marinated in chipotle <a href="/wiki/Adobo" title="Adobo">adobo</a>, at six locations in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The flour tortillas used for the burritos and soft tacos are the only items that contain gluten.<sup id="cite_ref-special_137-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-special-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_sourcing">Food sourcing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Food sourcing" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 1999, while looking for ways to improve the taste of the carnitas,<sup id="cite_ref-parrish_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parrish-20">[20]</a></sup> Steve Ells was prompted by an article written by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Behr_(food_writer)" title="Edward Behr (food writer)">Edward Behr</a> to visit <a href="/wiki/Concentrated_Animal_Feeding_Operation" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentrated Animal Feeding Operation">Concentrated Animal Feeding Operations</a> (CAFOs).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Ells found the CAFOs "horrific", and began sourcing from open-range pork suppliers. This caused an increase in both the price and the sales of the carnitas burritos.<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>In 2001, Chipotle released a <a href="/wiki/Mission_statement" title="Mission statement">mission statement</a> called <i>Food With Integrity</i>, which highlighted Chipotle's efforts to increase their use of naturally raised meat, <a href="/wiki/Organic_food" title="Organic food">organic produce</a>, and dairy without added <a href="/wiki/Hormone" title="Hormone">hormones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-barnes_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barnes-7">[7]</a></sup> Chipotle only uses the leg and thigh meat from its chickens; the breast meat is sold to <a href="/wiki/Panera_Bread" title="Panera Bread">Panera Bread</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UMW_students_at_a_Chipotle_in_Fredericksburg,_VA,_near_campus.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/UMW_students_at_a_Chipotle_in_Fredericksburg%2C_VA%2C_near_campus.jpg/220px-UMW_students_at_a_Chipotle_in_Fredericksburg%2C_VA%2C_near_campus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 124px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/UMW_students_at_a_Chipotle_in_Fredericksburg%2C_VA%2C_near_campus.jpg/220px-UMW_students_at_a_Chipotle_in_Fredericksburg%2C_VA%2C_near_campus.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="124" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UMW_students_at_a_Chipotle_in_Fredericksburg,_VA,_near_campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Customers at a Chipotle restaurant in Fredericksburg, Virginia</div></div></div>
<p>Founder Steve Ells has testified before the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> in support of the Preservation of Antibiotics for Medical Treatment Act, which aims to reduce the amount of antibiotics given to farm animals.<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>Since 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Coalition_of_Immokalee_Workers" title="Coalition of Immokalee Workers">Coalition of Immokalee Workers</a> (CIW), a Floridian farmworker organization, has protested Chipotle's refusal to sign a Fair Food agreement, which would commit the restaurant chain to pay a penny-per-pound premium on its Florida tomatoes to boost tomato harvesters' wages, and to only buy Florida tomatoes from growers who comply with the Fair Food Code of Conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> In 2009, the creators of the documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Food,_Inc." title="Food, Inc.">Food, Inc.</a></i> (along with 31 other leaders in the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_food_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Sustainable food systems">sustainable food</a> movement) signed an open letter of support for the CIW's campaign, stating that, "If Chipotle is sincere in its wishes to reform its supply chain, the time has come to work with the Coalition of Immokalee Workers as a true partner in the protection of farmworkers rights."<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In September 2009, Chipotle announced that it would sidestep partnership with the CIW and instead work directly with East Coast Growers and Packers to increase wages for its tomato pickers.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> CEO Steve Ells has framed the dispute as a fundamental issue of control, stating that, "the CIW wants us to sign a contract that would let them control Chipotle's decisions regarding food in the future."<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> In October 2012, Chipotle Mexican Grill signed an agreement with the CIW and became the 11th company to join the organization's Fair Food Program.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2015, Chipotle pulled carnitas from its menu in a third of its restaurants; company officials cited animal welfare problems at one of the suppliers, found during a regular audit, as the reason.<sup id="cite_ref-ferdman_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferdman-149">[149]</a></sup> Subsequently, a false rumor spread online claiming it was done to appease Muslims who consider pork to be unclean, leading to some protests on social media.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The company still uses antibiotic-free and hormone-free steak in its restaurants, despite being briefly forced to "serve beef that is not naturally raised" during the summer of 2013, posting an in-store notice each time that occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Roberto Ferdman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> opined that Chipotle's stated mission to sell "food with integrity" may be "untenable" if meat producers continue to breach Chipotle's ethical standards.<sup id="cite_ref-ferdman_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferdman-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>Also in 2015, Chipotle stopped using <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_organism" title="Genetically modified organism">genetically modified</a> corn and soy beans in their foods, claiming to be the first nationwide restaurant to cook completely GMO free.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>  This was done in response to increasing consumer demand for GMO free products.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_safety">Food safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Food safety" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 250px; float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em"><caption>External video</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 16px;height: 16px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="16" data-height="16" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x"> </span> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0oJ6cYyr1bQ">"How Chipotle made hundreds of people barf"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Vox_(website)" title="Vox (website)">Vox</a></i> report dated January 6, 2016, explaining Chipotle's "food safety crisis".</td></tr></tbody></table><p>Since 2008, a former <a href="/wiki/Kansas_State_University" title="Kansas State University">Kansas State University</a> food safety professor has accused Chipotle of confusing the public by using such terms as "naturally raised meats", "organic ingredients", and "locally sourced" and trying to equate those terms with food safety.<sup id="cite_ref-tdb-2015dec11_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdb-2015dec11-153">[153]</a></sup> In rebuttal, a Chipotle spokesperson told <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> that "all of our practices have always been very much within industry norms. It's important to note that restaurant practices are regulated by health codes, and restaurants are routinely inspected by health officials. Everything we have done in our supply chain and in our restaurants has been within industry norms."<sup id="cite_ref-tdb-2015dec11_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdb-2015dec11-153">[153]</a></sup> Yet, <a href="/wiki/FiveThirtyEight" title="FiveThirtyEight">FiveThirtyEight</a> pointed out that the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Norovirus" title="Norovirus">norovirus</a> outbreak appears to be unusual<sup id="cite_ref-fivethirtyeight-2015dec10_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fivethirtyeight-2015dec10-154">[154]</a></sup> and others are criticizing their food sourcing or handling practices.<sup id="cite_ref-vw-2015dec12_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vw-2015dec12-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyp-2015dec11_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyp-2015dec11-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MarketWatch" title="MarketWatch">MarketWatch</a> wrote that the result of all of these outbreaks will be to force Chipotle to obtain their produce from larger corporate farms that can afford the more extensive microbial food-safety testing programs and to process vegetables at centralized locations instead of at the individual stores, both of which are industry-standard practices that the company had previously criticized.<sup id="cite_ref-marketwatch-2015dec15_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketwatch-2015dec15-157">[157]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> implied that the company's insistence on maintaining its long standing rhetoric about "food integrity" seemed to be quite opposite with the realities of recent current events and made it appear that the management was just ignoring their current problems.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2015dec21_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2015dec21-158">[158]</a></sup> It also has been pointed out that Chipotle's current record-keeping system is actually hindering the health authorities' investigation in locating the sources of the various infections.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2015dec21_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2015dec21-158">[158]</a></sup></p><p>A writer for the magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Popular_Science" title="Popular Science">Popular Science</a></i> pointed out that Chipotle had publicly acknowledged that they "may be at a higher risk for food-borne illness outbreaks than some competitors due to our use of fresh produce and meats rather than frozen, and our reliance on employees cooking with traditional methods rather than automation."<sup id="cite_ref-ps-2015dec17_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps-2015dec17-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henry_I._Miller" title="Henry I. Miller">Henry I. Miller</a>, a medical researcher and columnist and the founding director of the FDA's Office of Biotechnology, asked: "One wonders whether Chipotle’s "traditional methods" include employees' neglecting to wash their hands before preparing food, which is how norovirus is usually spread. And the fresh versus frozen dichotomy is nothing more than a snow-job. Freezing <i>E. coli</i>-contaminated food does not kill the pathogens; it preserves them."<sup id="cite_ref-miller_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller-162">[162]</a></sup> Describing food poisoning outbreaks as "something of a Chipotle trademark; the recent ones are the fourth and fifth this year [2015], one of which was not disclosed to the public", Miller notes that "a particularly worrisome aspect of the company's serial deficiencies is that there have been at least three unrelated pathogens in the outbreaks – Salmonella and <i>E. coli</i> bacteria and norovirus. In other words, there has been more than a single glitch; suppliers and employees have found a variety of ways to contaminate what Chipotle cavalierly sells (at premium prices) to its customers."<sup id="cite_ref-miller_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller-162">[162]</a></sup></p><p>A writer for the North Carolina newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_News_%26_Observer" title="The News &amp; Observer">The News &amp; Observer</a></i> called Chipotle's "food with integrity" a "lucrative farce" and a "marketing ploy" by pointing out that organic food is "often grown with manure (an 'all-natural' fertilizer), which can certainly increase the risks of accidentally spreading fecal bacteria like <i><a href="/wiki/E._coli" class="mw-redirect" title="E. coli">E. coli</a></i>."<sup id="cite_ref-tno-2016jan08_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tno-2016jan08-163">[163]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2015, Seattle health officials closed a Seattle-area Chipotle for a day after it had repeatedly had small numbers of violations during recent consecutive inspections that previously would not have generated a closure order.<sup id="cite_ref-st-2015dec10_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-2015dec10-164">[164]</a></sup> On December 10, 2015, CEO Steve Ells released a press statement apologizing for 2015 outbreaks and promised changes to minimize the risks of future outbreaks.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="March_2008_hepatitis_outbreak">March 2008 hepatitis outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: March 2008 hepatitis outbreak" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In March and April 2008, the Community Epidemiology Branch of the San Diego County Health and Human Services Agency traced a <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_A" title="Hepatitis A">hepatitis A</a> outbreak in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County,_California" title="San Diego County, California">San Diego County</a> to a single Chipotle restaurant located in <a href="/wiki/La_Mesa,_California" title="La Mesa, California">La Mesa, California</a> in which 22 customers were infected with the virus.<sup id="cite_ref-sdc-2008may05_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sdc-2008may05-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kgtv-2008jun18_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kgtv-2008jun18-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="April_2008_norovirus_outbreak">April 2008 norovirus outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: April 2008 norovirus outbreak" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, Chipotle was implicated in a <a href="/wiki/Norovirus" title="Norovirus">norovirus</a> outbreak in <a href="/wiki/Kent,_Ohio" title="Kent, Ohio">Kent, Ohio</a>, where over 400 people became ill after eating at a Chipotle restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Officials at the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Department_of_Health" title="Ohio Department of Health">Ohio Department of Health</a> said that the outbreak was caused by <i>Norovirus Genotype G2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-woio-2008apr28_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-woio-2008apr28-169">[169]</a></sup> Many of the victims were students at <a href="/wiki/Kent_State_University" title="Kent State University">Kent State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-abj-2008apr18_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abj-2008apr18-170">[170]</a></sup> The initial source of the outbreak was never found.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="February_2009_Campylobacter_jejuni_outbreak">February 2009 <i>Campylobacter jejuni</i> outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: February 2009 Campylobacter jejuni outbreak" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Department_of_Health" title="Minnesota Department of Health">Minnesota Department of Health</a> traced an outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Campylobacter_jejuni" title="Campylobacter jejuni">campylobacteriosis</a> to a Chipotle Mexican Grill in <a href="/wiki/Apple_Valley,_Minnesota" title="Apple Valley, Minnesota">Apple Valley, Minnesota</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> The investigation found that chicken was sometimes served undercooked by the restaurant and determined that lettuce which had been cross-contaminated with raw or undercooked chicken was the vector for the outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Independent_sources" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Independent sources"><span title="A better source needed, Foodborne Illness Outbreak is written by Marler Clark LLP, who represent clients are suing Chipotle. According to the State of Minnesota report, raw chicken could just be likely. (January 2016)">third-party source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="July_2015_E._coli_outbreak">July 2015 <i>E. coli</i> outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: July 2015 E. coli outbreak" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In early November 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oregonian" title="The Oregonian">The Oregonian</a></i> reported that there was a little-known <i>E. coli</i> outbreak that had occurred earlier in July in which five people were infected with the <a href="/wiki/Escherichia_coli_O157:H7" title="Escherichia coli O157:H7">O157:H7 strain of <i>E. coli</i></a>. The outbreak was traced to a single Chipotle location in Seattle and that the incident was not publicized at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-to-2015nov10_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-2015nov10-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-st-2015nov05_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-2015nov05-177">[177]</a></sup> Seattle public health officials defended their actions at that time by saying that the outbreak was over by the time they made an association with Chipotle. Health officials were unable to trace the source of the July outbreak and said that the cause of the July outbreak is unrelated to the October/November outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-to-2015nov10_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-2015nov10-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="August_2015_norovirus_outbreak">August 2015 norovirus outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: August 2015 norovirus outbreak" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Another norovirus outbreak was confirmed to have occurred in August 2015 at a <a href="/wiki/Simi_Valley,_California" title="Simi Valley, California">Simi Valley, California</a> location in which 80 customers and 18 employees reported becoming ill.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-2015sep04_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-2015sep04-178">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-knbc-2015sep04_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knbc-2015sep04-179">[179]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ventura_County,_California" title="Ventura County, California">Ventura County</a> health inspectors found various health violations during two inspections following the outbreak report.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Despite those violations, the county health officials did not close the restaurant and allowed it to continue to operate.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-2015sep04_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-2015sep04-178">[178]</a></sup> In a January 2016 article, <i>The New York Times</i> reported that the number of victims involved in the Simi Valley norovirus outbreak was actually 207, twice the number that was reported earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2016jan06_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2016jan06-181">[181]</a></sup></p><p>In an unusual move, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Attorney" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Attorney">U.S. Attorney</a>'s Office for the Central District of California in conjunction with the Food and Drug Administration has gotten a <a href="/wiki/Federal_grand_jury" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal grand jury">federal grand jury</a> to issue a subpoena in January 2016 as part of a criminal investigation seeking documents and information from Chipotle concerning the Simi Valley norovirus outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2016jan06_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2016jan06-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lat-2016jan06_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-2016jan06-182">[182]</a></sup> As of January 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it is too early to tell which organization is the actual target of the investigation. In most cases involving norovirus outbreaks that involved a single location, state and/or local authorities are the usual jurisdiction responsible in the investigation and prosecution of those type of cases.  However, Ventura County officials had been criticized for their handling of parts of their investigation, and for allowing the restaurant to continue to operate after finding health violations during consecutive inspections.
</p><p>Less than two weeks later, a federal class action lawsuit was filed in the U.S. District Court for the Central District of California claiming that Chipotle knowingly allowed an ill kitchen manager to work for two days before sending that person home. Then, the restaurant actively deep-cleaned the restaurant to remove all traces of contamination prior to notifying the Ventura County Environmental Health Division of the existing outbreak, hindering their investigation.  The lawsuit also claimed that the number of known victims was as high as 234 and estimates that the number of meals that the infected employee may have come in contact with could be as high 3,000.<sup id="cite_ref-vcs-2016jan19_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vcs-2016jan19-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eater-2016jan20_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2016jan20-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wnbc-2016jan20_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wnbc-2016jan20-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
