<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="August_2015_Salmonella_outbreak">August 2015 <i>Salmonella</i> outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: August 2015 Salmonella outbreak" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>At almost the same time as the Simi Valley norovirus outbreak, Minnesota health officials confirmed a <i><a href="/wiki/Salmonella" title="Salmonella">Salmonella</a></i> outbreak that affected 17 Minneapolis-area Chipotle restaurants in mid-August 2015. The source of the outbreak was traced back to contaminated tomatoes that were grown in Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-mst-2015sep11_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-2015sep11-186">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mst-2015sep16_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-2015sep16-187">[187]</a></sup> The Minnesota Department of Health reported that samples from 45 victims were tested and found that their illness was caused by the <i>Salmonella</i> Newport bacterium as determined by <a href="/wiki/DNA_profiling" title="DNA profiling">DNA profiling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mdoh-2015sep10_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdoh-2015sep10-188">[188]</a></sup> Later, the state officials reported that the total of persons who became infected was increased to 64 and the number Chipotle locations in which they had acquired the bacterium was increased to 22, all located within the state of Minnesota.<sup id="cite_ref-mdoh-2015sep16_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdoh-2015sep16-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="October_2015_E._coli_outbreak">October 2015 <i>E. coli</i> outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: October 2015 E. coli outbreak" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2015, at least 22 people were reported to have gotten sick after eating at several different Chipotle locations in the states of Washington and Oregon. At that time, an epidemiologist for the <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_Department_of_Health" title="Washington State Department of Health">Washington State Department of Health</a> said the culprit appeared to be a <a href="/wiki/Shiga_toxin" title="Shiga toxin">Shiga toxin</a>-producing <i><a href="/wiki/Escherichia_coli" title="Escherichia coli">Escherichia coli</a></i> bacterium, but they were still waiting the outcome of several laboratory tests before they could give a definitive result.<sup id="cite_ref-nn-2015oct31_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nn-2015oct31-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-st-2015oct31_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-2015oct31-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ut-2015oct31_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ut-2015oct31-192">[192]</a></sup> As a precaution, Chipotle had closed 43 stores in Washington and Oregon pending the results and recommendations of the involved health authorities. On November 5, the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a> (CDC) had reported that the number of persons reported ill had risen to 40 known cases and that the bacteria samples taken from 7 infected persons in Washington and 3 persons in Oregon states were confirmed to be infected by the same strain of <i>E. coli</i>, the Shiga toxin-producing STEC O26 strain, as determined by DNA profiling.<sup id="cite_ref-cfdcap-2015nov05_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfdcap-2015nov05-193">[193]</a></sup> At least 12 persons required hospitalization, but no fatalities. As of November 2015, Health authorities were still trying to trace the exact source of the bacterial contamination, but suspected fresh produce.<sup id="cite_ref-st-2015nov04_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-2015nov04-194">[194]</a></sup></p><p>On November 12, the CDC increased the number of known cases to 50, the number of persons requiring hospitalization to 14, and the number of DNA fingerprint confirmations to 33.<sup id="cite_ref-cfdcap-2015nov12_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfdcap-2015nov12-195">[195]</a></sup> Through a match via <a href="/wiki/Pulsenet" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulsenet">Pulsenet</a>, the DNA fingerprint also matched a recent case in Minnesota, but the ill person did not eat at Chipotle. The source of the bacteria infection still had not yet been determined at the time of the report released by the CDC and the CDC is trying to use the more definitive, but more time-consuming <a href="/wiki/Whole_genome_sequencing" title="Whole genome sequencing">whole genome sequencing</a> procedure to see if they are able to determine the relationships between all of the STEC O26 cases. In the meantime, Chipotle reopened the closed restaurants on November 11 after disposing all of the food within the closed facilities and deep cleaning those facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-nbc-2015nov11_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbc-2015nov11-196">[196]</a></sup></p><p>On November 20, the CDC reported that the number of STEC O26 cases, as determined by DNA fingerprinting, had increased to 45 with 16 persons requiring hospitalization and the total number states being affected had increased to six.<sup id="cite_ref-cfdcap-2015nov20_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfdcap-2015nov20-197">[197]</a></sup> Besides Oregon and Washington, new cases were reported in the states of Minnesota, California, New York, and Ohio.<sup id="cite_ref-nyp-2015nov21_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyp-2015nov21-198">[198]</a></sup> 43 out of 45 of the affected individuals had reported that they had eaten at a Chipotle in the week before they had become sick.
</p><p>On December 4, the CDC reported that the number of STEC O26 cases, as determined by DNA fingerprinting, had increased to 52 with 20 persons requiring hospitalization and the total number states being affected had increased to nine.<sup id="cite_ref-cfdcap-2015dec04_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfdcap-2015dec04-199">[199]</a></sup> New cases were reported in the states of California (1), Illinois (1), Maryland (1), Ohio (2), Pennsylvania (1), and Washington (1).<sup id="cite_ref-hp-2015dec04_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hp-2015dec04-200">[200]</a></sup></p><p>The price of shares for Chipotle stock dropped a further 12% immediately after the CDC had issued their update on November 20.<sup id="cite_ref-tmf-2015nov20_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmf-2015nov20-201">[201]</a></sup> Share prices had been dropping since the initial announcement of the <i>E. coli</i> outbreak in late October with investors unsure if the drop in share prices just a temporary aberration and that Chipotle management is handling the incident as well as they could. Chipotle has since hired a consultant to improve their food safety program and have their program reviewed by both the CDC and FDA.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes-2015dec04_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-2015dec04-202">[202]</a></sup></p><p>On February 1, 2016, the CDC official closed their investigations on the larger <i>E. coli</i> that started in Pacific Northwest in October 2015 and also the smaller outbreak that started in Kansas and Oklahoma in November since no new cases were reported since December 1.<sup id="cite_ref-cfdcap-2016feb01_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfdcap-2016feb01-203">[203]</a></sup> In their final report, the CDC stated that 55 persons in 11 states were infected with the same strain of STEC O26 during the major outbreak with 21 of those persons requiring hospitalization. The five persons infected in the later outbreak were made ill by a <a href="/wiki/Genetically" class="mw-redirect" title="Genetically">genetically</a> different strain of STEC O26. The CDC also reported that federal and local health and food safety authorities were unable to detect traces of the microorganisms in any of the food samples taken from the suspected restaurants or from their supply chain. The CDC, FDA, and the USDA Food Safety and Inspection Service were unable to determine a point source that was in common in the meals that were consumed by all the victims since some of the restaurants were located far apart and had obtained some of their ingredients from different suppliers while other consumers of the suspected suppliers were not affected.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="November_2015_E._coli_cases">November 2015 <i>E. coli</i> cases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: November 2015 E. coli cases" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Centers for Disease Control and Prevention reported on December 21 that five more people became ill after eating at two Chipotle restaurants located in Kansas and Oklahoma in late November. Preliminary DNA fingerprinting results appear to indicated that the newer cases were caused by a different strain of Shiga toxin-producing <i>E. coli</i> O26. Scientists are waiting for the results of the more definitive whole genome sequencing analyses to determine if the organisms responsible for this outbreak are genetically related to the <i>E. coli</i> that are responsible for causing the outbreak that had started in Oregon and Washington in late October and thus an extension of that outbreak.  The agency has not yet determined which food is responsible for the outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-cfdcap-2015dec22_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfdcap-2015dec22-204">[204]</a></sup> The Food and Drug Administration reported that they are trying to determine how the bacteria in these cases, along with the earlier Oregon, Washington, and other multi-state cases, might have been propagated through the food supply chain.<sup id="cite_ref-fda-2015dec21_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fda-2015dec21-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="December_2015_norovirus_outbreak">December 2015 norovirus outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: December 2015 norovirus outbreak" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Cleveland_Circle,_December_2015.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Cleveland_Circle%2C_December_2015.JPG/220px-Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Cleveland_Circle%2C_December_2015.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Cleveland_Circle%2C_December_2015.JPG/220px-Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Cleveland_Circle%2C_December_2015.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Cleveland_Circle,_December_2015.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The closed restaurant on December 16, 2015</div></div></div>
<p>In December 2015, eighty students at <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>, including members of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_College_Eagles_men%27s_basketball" title="Boston College Eagles men's basketball">men's basketball</a> team, were sickened after eating at a single Chipotle restaurant. Affected students had been tested for both <i>E. coli</i> and norovirus in order to determine the cause of the illnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-pj20151207_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pj20151207-206">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Although it would take as long as two days before the results of more definitive tests became known, public health investigators reported that preliminary tests pointed to the presence of norovirus.<sup id="cite_ref-nn-2015dec08_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nn-2015dec08-208">[208]</a></sup> The health inspectors for the City of Boston had since closed this particular location on December 7 for a number of health violations that included maintaining meats at a too low of a temperature on the serving line and for allowing a sick employee to work at the time of the inspection.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p><p>On December 10, officials from the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Public_Health_Commission" title="Boston Public Health Commission">Boston Public Health Commission</a> reported that tests had identified a single strain of norovirus that is responsible for this particular outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-wbur-2015dec10_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wbur-2015dec10-210">[210]</a></sup> Boston Globe reported on December 10 that 141 persons were reported to have gotten ill and that some of the newer victims had not visited Chipotle before contracting the virus<sup id="cite_ref-bg-2015dec10_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bg-2015dec10-211">[211]</a></sup> and most likely became infected by being in close proximity to someone who had gotten ill at Chipotle, such as a roommate or dorm-mate.<sup id="cite_ref-wbur-2015dec10_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wbur-2015dec10-210">[210]</a></sup> Boston authorities traced the cause of the outbreak to a sick employee who was allowed to work on the day of the outbreak. Chipotle has since fired the employee and also the manager who knowingly allowed the ill worker to complete his shift instead of following health codes.<sup id="cite_ref-wcvb-tv-2015dec23_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wcvb-tv-2015dec23-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Consequences_of_the_multiple_incidents_in_2015">Consequences of the multiple incidents in 2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Consequences of the multiple incidents in 2015" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On February 8, 2016, Chipotle closed all of its eateries nationwide for a few hours during the morning for an all-staff meeting on food safety.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> The company hired a new head of food safety, who instituted changes including having all employees wash hands every half hour, having two employees verify that produce like onions, jalapeños and avocados have been immersed in hot water for five seconds to kill germs on their exteriors, and using <a href="/wiki/Pascalization" title="Pascalization">Pascalization</a> to pre-treat food ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-strom20160922_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strom20160922-214">[214]</a></sup></p><p>Since the series of food-poisoning outbreaks in 2015 lowered trust in the product, Chipotle has tried to lure back its customers with free food and heavier advertising. Same-store sales increased 17.8% percent in the first quarter of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="July_2017_norovirus_outbreak">July 2017 norovirus outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: July 2017 norovirus outbreak" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Despite corrective actions, the company faced another setback in implementing their safe food policies in July 2017.  A norovirus outbreak is being investigated in Virginia.  More than 130 people reported having norovirus-like symptoms and two individuals had tested positive for the virus after eating at a Chipotle restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Sterling,_Virginia" title="Sterling, Virginia">Sterling, Virginia</a>.  The Loudoun County Health Department confirmed the illnesses from July 13–16, 2017.  Shares of Chipotle's stock stumbled more than 10% on this news<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> and also the news that customers had posted videos of mice skittering through a Chipotle restaurant in Dallas just a few days before the norovirus incident was reported.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn-2017jul20_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-2017jul20-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn-2017jul26_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-2017jul26-219">[219]</a></sup> On July 25, several news agencies reported that Chipotle officials confirmed that the "recent norovirus outbreak in Virginia was the result of lax sick policy enforcement by store managers" and that the company believed that an employee was the cause of the outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc-2017jul25_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc-2017jul25-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn-2017jul26_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-2017jul26-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="July_2018_Clostridium_perfringens_outbreak">July 2018 <i>Clostridium perfringens</i> outbreak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: July 2018 Clostridium perfringens outbreak" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In late July 2018, Ohio public health officials launched an investigation after receiving 368 complaints from customers after they had eaten at a <a href="/wiki/Powell,_Ohio" title="Powell, Ohio">Powell, Ohio</a>, location.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> By mid-August, the U.S. Center for Disease Control identified the bacteria that cause the outbreak which had affected over 700 people as <i><a href="/wiki/Clostridium_perfringens" title="Clostridium perfringens">Clostridium perfringens</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc-2018aug16_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc-2018aug16-222">[222]</a></sup> This food borne outbreak has been called the worst incident to date that can be traced to a single restaurant location.<sup id="cite_ref-delish-2018aug20_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delish-2018aug20-223">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-refinery29-2018aug08_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-refinery29-2018aug08-224">[224]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_breaches">Data breaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Data breaches" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>Chipotle had two known incidents in which customer credit card payment information was stolen.<sup id="cite_ref-kmgh-tv-2017may19_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kmgh-tv-2017may19-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2004_data_breach">2004 data breach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 2004 data breach" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In May 2006, Chipotle filed a report with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission that the company may have experience theft of credit and debit card data that might have existed as far back as 1999, when the company first accepted credit and debit cards as payment, until August 2004 when the merchant bank that process their credit and debit card transactions had informed Chipotle of the possible theft of credit and debit card information. Although the Chipotle claimed that there was no proof that theft of credit and debit card information had actually occurred, the results of outside forensic auditing firms concluded that the company's use of flawed card processing software and the use of unsecured internet gateways by some of their computers may have made their information systems at the affected restaurants vulnerable during periods before August 2004. The company spent $5.5 million to settle legal claims, and pay fines and related legal fees.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> The general public was not informed of the company's <a href="/wiki/Data_security" title="Data security">data security</a> problems when the company first became aware of the situation.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_data_breach">2017 data breach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 2017 data breach" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In April 2017, Chipotle first announced that their <a href="/wiki/Point_of_sale" title="Point of sale">point of sale</a> payment system was compromised during a three-week period from late March to mid-April but gave very little information about the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-fm-2017apr25_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fm-2017apr25-227">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sm-2017apr26_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sm-2017apr26-228">[228]</a></sup> The following month, the company later revealed that 2,250 restaurants in 47 states were involved which could potentially affect hundreds of thousands of customers who may had their credit or debit card account information with security codes stolen.<sup id="cite_ref-eater-2017may30_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2017may30-229">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mrp-2017may29_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrp-2017may29-230">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-securityintelligence-2017jun01_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-securityintelligence-2017jun01-232">[232]</a></sup> A few restaurants in Canada were also affected.<sup id="cite_ref-tt-2017may27_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tt-2017may27-233">[233]</a></sup> Some security experts criticized the way Chipotle had downplayed the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-mrp-2017may29_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrp-2017may29-230">[230]</a></sup> During the same month, a credit union in New Hampshire filed a class action lawsuit on the behalf of banks and credit unions against Chipotle for failure to provide elementary credit card data security in the most recent <a href="/wiki/Data_breach" title="Data breach">data breach</a> after a similar data breach that had occurred in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-kmgh-tv-2017may19_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kmgh-tv-2017may19-225">[225]</a></sup> In July 2017, <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville, Florida</a>, police reported that an unidentified person took more than $17,000 from an <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">ATM</a> at a local credit union by stealing from 40 different accounts that can be traced directly to the data breach.<sup id="cite_ref-osb-2017jul20_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osb-2017jul20-234">[234]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sm-2017jul21_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sm-2017jul21-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Lawsuits">Lawsuits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Lawsuits" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>In November 2016, three men filed a <a href="/wiki/Class-action_lawsuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Class-action lawsuit">class-action lawsuit</a> against Chipotle alleging that a burrito was listed as containing only 300 calories, when in fact it contained more. They are seeking "unspecified damages and for an injunction against the company to prevent it from posting what it calls misleading information on its food."<sup id="cite_ref-lawsuit1_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lawsuit1-236">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lawsuit2_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lawsuit2-237">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lawsuit3_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lawsuit3-238">[238]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2020 the company received a $1.3 million fine from the state of Massachusetts for 13,000 <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">child labor</a> violations.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising_and_publicity">Advertising and publicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Advertising and publicity" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_free_burrito_day.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Chipotle_free_burrito_day.jpg/220px-Chipotle_free_burrito_day.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2892" data-file-height="2200"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 167px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Chipotle_free_burrito_day.jpg/220px-Chipotle_free_burrito_day.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="167" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_free_burrito_day.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People line up outside a Chipotle in <a href="/wiki/East_Lansing,_Michigan" title="East Lansing, Michigan">East Lansing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> during a "Free Burrito Day"</div></div></div>
<p>In the past, Chipotle mainly relied on billboards, radio ads, and <a href="/wiki/Word_of_mouth" title="Word of mouth">word of mouth</a> to advertise.<sup id="cite_ref-buzz_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buzz-31">[31]</a></sup> In 2012, Chipotle aired its first nationally televised commercial during the <a href="/wiki/54th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Annual Grammy Awards">54th Annual Grammy Awards</a> ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> In 2010, the company initiated an ad campaign that mocks advice given to Chipotle by advertising agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Chipotle has run many promotions giving out free food to potential customers, especially when opening a new store. Stores also give out free burritos on certain holidays; for instance, on <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a>, some locations have had promotions in which free burritos are given to people who come dressed as a burrito. Chipotle gave away free burritos to reporters during the 1997 trial of <a href="/wiki/Timothy_McVeigh" title="Timothy McVeigh">Timothy McVeigh</a>, which took place in Chipotle's hometown of Denver.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> In addition, stores offered free burritos to those displaced by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> Chipotle received attention when <a href="/wiki/Ozzy_Osbourne" title="Ozzy Osbourne">Ozzy Osbourne</a>'s reality show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Osbournes" title="The Osbournes">The Osbournes</a></i> featured the company's burritos heavily.<sup id="cite_ref-rocky2-feeding_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rocky2-feeding-29">[29]</a></sup> For Halloween 2010, Chipotle announced that customers dressed as a processed food product would receive a burrito for $2. The event was part of a $1 million fundraiser for <i><a href="/wiki/Jamie_Oliver%27s_Food_Revolution" title="Jamie Oliver's Food Revolution">Jamie Oliver's Food Revolution</a></i> called "Boorito 2010: The Horrors of Processed Food."<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> For "Boorito 2011", customers dressed in costumes "inspired by family farms" will receive a menu item for $2, with proceeds from the promotion going to The Chipotle Cultivate Foundation and Farm Aid. The promotion is aimed to increase awareness of family farms.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> Also in support of family farms, Chipotle released music videos of <a href="/wiki/Karen_O" title="Karen O">Karen O</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Yeah_Yeah_Yeahs" title="Yeah Yeah Yeahs">Yeah Yeah Yeahs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson" title="Willie Nelson">Willie Nelson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> On September 12, 2013, Chipotle released an animated short called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scarecrow_(2013_film)" title="The Scarecrow (2013 film)">The Scarecrow</a></i>, with a companion mobile video game; both feature a narrative heavily critical of <a href="/wiki/Intensive_farming" title="Intensive farming">industrial farming</a>, but little in the way of direct marketing for the chain.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> The short features a cover of "<a href="/wiki/Pure_Imagination" title="Pure Imagination">Pure Imagination</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/Willy_Wonka_%26_the_Chocolate_Factory" title="Willy Wonka &amp; the Chocolate Factory">Willy Wonka &amp; the Chocolate Factory</a></i>, sung by <a href="/wiki/Fiona_Apple" title="Fiona Apple">Fiona Apple</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup>  It was named one of the worst advertisements of 2013 by <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, Chipotle created the "Farm Team", which is a rewards program available only by invitation from restaurant managers. The Farm Team members have access to a special Chipotle website, where members can earn rewards, i.e. free food and T-shirts. The site offers members to, "learn where Chipotle’s food comes from, take quizzes and polls, play games and watch videos about the company".<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> In April 2014, the Farm Team program was shut down.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup></p><p>Chipotle sponsors Team Garmin-Barracuda (formerly Team Garmin-Chipotle, Team Garmin-Slipstream, Team Garmin-Transitions and Team Garmin-Cervélo) of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Cycliste_Internationale" title="Union Cycliste Internationale">International Cycling Union</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-velo_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-velo-254">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup>  and is an official team partner of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> In June 2009, Chipotle sponsored free screenings of <i><a href="/wiki/Food,_Inc." title="Food, Inc.">Food, Inc.</a></i>, a film that criticizes the corporate food industry. Founder Steve Ells stated that he hoped the film would make customers appreciate Chipotle's <i>Food With Integrity</i> policy.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> From May until September 2009, Chipotle ran a contest on mychipotle.com, a <a href="/wiki/Microsite" title="Microsite">microsite</a> which had a competition for the best user-created audio and video presentations about different combinations of ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> In July 2010, Chipotle began a campaign to support healthier lunch alternatives for students, in which money will be donated to The Lunch Box program based on how many spam E-mails consumers forward to a company E-mail address.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> For Chipotle's 18 year anniversary, the company began wrapping its burritos in gold foil as part of a larger promotion to draw attention to its <i>Food With Integrity</i> mantra.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> Also as part of the gold foil campaign, Chipotle is offering prizes for customer-created pictures of items wrapped in gold foil. Chipotle hired comedian <a href="/wiki/Amy_Sedaris" title="Amy Sedaris">Amy Sedaris</a> to create a comedic how-to video on wrapping with gold foil, and spread the video using <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> In March 2013, Chipotle pulled its sponsorship of a <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America" title="Boy Scouts of America">Boy Scouts of America</a> event, citing that organization's <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America_membership_controversies" title="Boy Scouts of America membership controversies">ban on LGBT members</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Cultivating_Thought.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Chipotle_Cultivating_Thought.jpg/170px-Chipotle_Cultivating_Thought.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 227px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Chipotle_Cultivating_Thought.jpg/170px-Chipotle_Cultivating_Thought.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="227" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chipotle_Cultivating_Thought.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cup and bag from the "Cultivating Thought" series, featuring the work of Paulo Coelho and Augusten Burroughs</div></div></div>
<p>On December 16, 2015, Chipotle ran full page ads in both <a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Herald" title="Boston Herald">Boston Herald</a> apologizing for the recent norovirus outbreak linked to Chipotle's Cleveland Circle location. The ad, containing a letter by Chipotle founder and co-CEO Steve Ells, affirmed the company's commitment to food safety.<sup id="cite_ref-bg-2015dec16_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bg-2015dec16-265">[265]</a></sup></p><p>On March 14, 2016, a <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Board" title="National Labor Relations Board">National Labor Relations Board</a> (NLRB) administrative law judge concluded that Chipotle's social media policy, and more specifically its application towards an employee who posted tweets regarding wages and working conditions, violated the <a href="/wiki/National_Labor_Relations_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="National Labor Relations Act">National Labor Relations Act</a> (NLRA).<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> A former Chipotle employee in <a href="/wiki/Havertown,_Pennsylvania" title="Havertown, Pennsylvania">Havertown, Pennsylvania</a>, wrote a series of tweets from his personal account about hourly workers being required to work on snow days. Chipotle instructed the employee to delete the tweets. The NLRB judge determined that Chipotle's request to delete the tweets violated the NLRA even though the employee was not disciplined as a result of his tweets.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Architecture" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-10-05_Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Durham_new.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/2008-10-05_Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Durham_new.jpg/220px-2008-10-05_Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Durham_new.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="453" data-file-height="397"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 193px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/2008-10-05_Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Durham_new.jpg/220px-2008-10-05_Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Durham_new.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="193" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-10-05_Chipotle_Mexican_Grill_in_Durham_new.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The exterior of a Chipotle in <a href="/wiki/Durham,_North_Carolina" title="Durham, North Carolina">Durham, North Carolina</a></div></div></div>
<p>Architecturally, all Chipotle restaurants are built using most of the same materials (plywood, corrugated metal, stainless steel, exposed ductwork), although each store is unique.<sup id="cite_ref-parrish_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parrish-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ells_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ells-268">[268]</a></sup> The interiors have been described as having an "industrial, sheet metal look".<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> Chipotle has built restaurants using white ceramic tile instead of stainless steel.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> It costs the company approximately $850,000 to open a new restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> When the first Chipotle opened, Steve Ells asked his friend, sculptor Bruce Gueswel, to design the chairs and a styled Mayan king whose face was loosely based on that of civil rights leader <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a>, a personal inspiration of Gueswel, for the restaurant. Both items were made from wood and metal. Gueswel has continued to design and build the art and chairs for all subsequent Chipotle restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup></p><p>Most Chipotle locations display a photograph of the original restaurant, which is near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a> campus on Evans Avenue.<sup id="cite_ref-parrish_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parrish-20">[20]</a></sup> Instead of a photograph of itself, the original location has a photograph of the Dolly Madison Ice Cream that previously occupied the location. In 2010, Chipotle began opening smaller concept locations that have lower costs of development and occupancy.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup> Chipotle uses environmentally friendly packaging, with bowls made from recycled newsprint, unbleached tray liners, and napkins and cups made from postconsumer waste.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup></p><p>Chipotle's architectural design team incorporates the principles of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_architecture" title="Sustainable architecture">sustainable architecture</a> in their projects. The "green" restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Gurnee,_Illinois" title="Gurnee, Illinois">Gurnee, Illinois</a> features an on-site six kilowatt wind turbine, which generates about 10% of the restaurant's electrical needs. The Gurnee restaurant has received Platinum level <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> certification from <a href="/wiki/U.S._Green_Building_Council" title="U.S. Green Building Council">U.S. Green Building Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pundit_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pundit-275">[275]</a></sup> A restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Tulsa,_Oklahoma" title="Tulsa, Oklahoma">Tulsa</a>, Oklahoma, uses recycled drywall, low-<a href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compound" title="Volatile organic compound">VOC</a> paint, and energy-efficient appliances.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> A Chipotle restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a> was the first to receive a four-star rating from the city's Green Building Program.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> Additionally, Chipotle has made arrangements to add <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">solar panels</a> to 75 of its restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-pundit_275-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pundit-275">[275]</a></sup> Chipotle has contracted to clean its stores in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, with "plant-based, environmentally preferable cleaning supplies and technologies." The cleansers are readily biodegradable and non-toxic to humans or aquatic life.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup></p><p>Chipotle was the defendant in a lawsuit for failure to comply with the <a href="/wiki/Americans_with_Disabilities_Act_of_1990" title="Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990">Americans with Disabilities Act</a> (ADA). <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Antoninetti" title="Maurizio Antoninetti">Maurizio Antoninetti</a>, a customer who used a wheelchair, claimed he was denied the "Chipotle Experience", because he was unable to see the food preparation. The case against the company was upheld in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Ninth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ADA_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADA-279">[279]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> declined to hear Chipotle's appeal, leaving the Ninth Circuit's ruling intact.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> Chipotle has "an official disability policy of bringing ingredients to the tables of diners with disabilities and doing tableside preparation." Chipotle is retrofitting restaurants affected by the ruling, replacing the walls in front of the food preparation area with lower ones or transparent panels. They are incorporating the new design elements into new restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-ADA_279-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADA-279">[279]</a></sup> The case was one of over twenty ADA-related lawsuits filed by Antoninetti, who died in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-ADA_279-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADA-279">[279]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_restaurant_units">Other restaurant units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Other restaurant units" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<p><span id="Pizzeria_Locale"></span>
</p>
<ul><li>Pizzeria Locale is a fast casual pizza restaurant formed as a partnership with Pizzeria Locale, a full-service pizza restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder, Colorado</a>. The original Pizzeria Locale owners, Bobby Stuckey and Lachlan Mackinnon-Patterson, would continue to own their original location while Chipotle would increase its stake in the chain over time.<sup id="cite_ref-nmx_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmx-60">[60]</a></sup> By February 2017, the chain had grown to seven locations.<sup id="cite_ref-lat_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-63">[63]</a></sup> In June 2018, Chipotle closed five Pizzeria Locale locations in Kansas City and Cincinnati, leaving two locations in Denver and one in Boulder still opened.<sup id="cite_ref-eater-2018jun27_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2018jun27-282">[282]</a></sup> In March 2019, Pizzeria Locale announced plans but no schedule to open two additional locations within the Denver metropolitan area, one in <a href="/wiki/Hale,_Colorado" title="Hale, Colorado">Hale</a> and the other in <a href="/wiki/Stapleton,_Denver" title="Stapleton, Denver">Stapleton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-businessden-2019mar18_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businessden-2019mar18-283">[283]</a></sup></li></ul><dl><dt>Defunct Sub Companies</dt></dl><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Soul_Daddy" title="Soul Daddy">Soul Daddy</a> was a soul food fast casual restaurant that was owned by ANGR Holdings, LLC, and was managed by Chipotle after purchasing Ellis' stake in the company. The restaurant had three locations that had operated for less than 5 weeks in 2011 before closing.<sup id="cite_ref-MOACLOSURE_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOACLOSURE-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ShopHouse_Southeast_Asian_Kitchen" title="ShopHouse Southeast Asian Kitchen">ShopHouse Southeast Asian Kitchen</a> was an <a href="/wiki/Asian_cuisine" title="Asian cuisine">Asian</a> fast-casual concept restaurant that was opened by Chipotle in September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-shophouse_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shophouse-57">[57]</a></sup> The company said that the new restaurant "would follow the Chipotle service format and its focus on 'food with integrity' in ingredients."<sup id="cite_ref-Jennings_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jennings-58">[58]</a></sup> Chipotle's plan was to start with only one store, and see how the restaurant works out before expanding the concept.<sup id="cite_ref-Anderson_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson-59">[59]</a></sup> By July 2016, the chain had 15 restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-lat_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-63">[63]</a></sup> All ShopHouse locations were closed on March 17, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-eater-2017mar09_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2017mar09-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tasty_Made" title="Tasty Made">Tasty Made</a> is a burger restaurant concept that Chipotle first opened in <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_Ohio" title="Lancaster, Ohio">Lancaster, Ohio</a> in October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> On July 29, 2016, the company announced the opening of its first Tasty Made burger restaurant in the fall. The first location was revealed to be in <a href="/wiki/Lancaster,_Ohio" title="Lancaster, Ohio">Lancaster, Ohio</a>. Ohio was selected as culinary manager Nate Appleman and national training director David Chrisman are both from the state and helped design the concept.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> Tasty Made was announced to have a focused menu like early burger restaurants which were limited to burgers, fries and milkshakes.<sup id="cite_ref-lat_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-63">[63]</a></sup> Chipotle had trademarked Better Burger earlier in the year. Tasty Made was closed on February 28, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-cbf-2018mar01_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbf-2018mar01-286">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eater-2018mar01_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eater-2018mar01-65">[65]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: References" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chipotle_Mexican_Grill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Further reading" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">
<ul><li><cite class="citation news">Berfield, Susan (December 22, 2015). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bloomberg.com/features/2015-chipotle-food-safety-crisis/">"Inside Chipotle's Contamination Crisis: Smugness and happy talk about sustainability aren't working anymore"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">Bloomberg Businessweek</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
